Jó játék. Első ránézésre könnyed játéknak tűnik, de egész komoly játék, van benne jócskán taktikai lehetőség. Ugyanakkor hátránya, hogy nagyon hosszú ideig tart. Másfél órás legalább a játékidő, és volt még ennél több is. 

Ennyi játékkal a hátam mögött már más a véleményem. Éppen, hogy gyorsan véget érhet a játék. A katakomba szerintem felesleges lap a játékban. Teljesen kiszámíthatatlanná teszi a játékot, nem tudni mikor ér véget. Hiába van jó kombinációt, ha valaki leépíti a Katakombát rögtön véget ér a játék. Másik nagy hiba a kézműves lap erőssége. Hiszen az épületet is tud kezdeni és hozzá építeni kézből. Míg az építész csak a raktárból tud, ahová csak a piacról tudunk munkással anyagot szerezni, azaz plusz egy kör a kézműveshez képest. Úgy kellene, hogy alapozni csak építésszel lehet és kézművessel már csak ahhoz tudnánk hozzáépíteni. Emiatt 8-ról, 7-re változtatom az értékelésemet.

RATING: 7
A variation on Race for the Galaxy/San Juan with the added complication that the same cards provide actions as well as materials and buildings. It's all fairly wild and wacky, the building powers are completely crazy and you can rack up stupid numbers of cards or actions. I'm no fan of the cartoony graphics in the first edition, but I suppose they go with the adolescent atmosphere of everything else. There's no point going in with a strategy, you've got to play the cards you get and take opportunities as they arise. Don't be deceived into thinking that this is a building game, it's in putting materials in your vault that the game is won and lost. Plenty of light fun here, but this isn't one to rank with the classics.

The recent Black Box edition is barely an improvement on the original. If you can get a copy without bubbles in the box wrap and staining on the player aids, the graphics are no more than clip art.

RATING: 7
My first impression of GtR was an overwhelmingly positive one. I enjoy the multifunctional use of cards which can be played as actions and discarded, used to create buildings, or used as permanent buffs that allow additional actions. Each building of 6 different suits can affect the game in many ways and allow for some pretty impressive power ups and combos. The game is quick to learn, but I can clearly see it will take me a long time to become familiar with all the possible routes to victory. One other aspect is the artwork, which is a gorgeously minimalist style. This low detail art may not appeal to everyone, but  I throughly enjoy it. There's a lot of terrific player interaction, and in the style of Race for the Galaxy or Puerto Rico, every action you choose allows others to take actions of the same type. GtR doesnt feel at all derivative however, and is a fresh take on the resource management, kingdom building genre.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Masterpiece: a card game which draws on the best parts of role selection games like San Juan, but really ups the interactiveness by giving players the option of whether to follow the role or to draw cards instead. Add in the extra layer of patronage, to get free uses of specific roles, and even the action system is highly open to manipulation and individual strategy. Once you get experienced with the game, that manipulation of actions and especially controlling the pool are absolutely central to the game - it makes it a truly competitive and head-to-head experience where you always have to pay attention to what your opponents are doing (which I so much prefer to multiplayer solitaire sort of games). And that's before you even mention the combos based on buildings! (My own favourite is the Sewer, which lets you put cards used to lead or follow straight into your stockpile: combined with the use of multiple cards as wilds, it gives you a truly formidable stockpile engine).
The only negatives are the fact that it's tricky to teach, and the occasional duff game when things don't quite click properly (for whatever reason). Also, in 2-player games (which most of mine are) the legionary is significantly less powerful - but I think the game's probably best with 3.

RATING: 8
A very fun card game.  Cards can be used in several different ways:  1) Build it as a building in your tableau for a powerful special ability, also you get victory points and increase your influence as well! 2) play it as a client to get extra actions 3) use cards as material to pay the construction cost of a building 4) stash cards in your vault for victory points at the end of the game.  Glory to Rome presents players with a rich variety of interesting options to choose from on their turn.  There are several different viable strategies you can try to win the game.  The game is also good because it is a stimulating, crunchy game, yet it doesn't take a very long time to play.  Glory to Rome can be a bit overwhelming for new players to learn, even serious gamers--yet, once you understand how it works, it is not an overly complicated game; it has a glaring elegance.  It does what it tries to do quite well.  It is interesting that the broad variety of buildings you may construct, some of them are crazy powerful and there are probably buildings that combo really well together--I do not yet know them yet as a relative newcomer to Glory to Rome.

RATING: 9.5
02/17/2016
From 8 to 9.5.

I just love this game. Why?

- Players are involved on every turn.

- Allows for creative play. I can work out what I want to do and often have multiple ways to achieve this. However, this is heavily influenced by what the other players are doing and one must quickly adapt.

- I can easily teach this. This game is an odd duck, but it clicks with me and I'm able to explain it well.

- The thematic tie ins between the building and their actions. I giggle when I think of the Coliseum or Bath and their abilities. Or the Sewer or Senate.

Things I don't like?

- Although can be taught easily, there is a learning curve regarding the brutality of some card combos and their counters.

- Availability. Yeah..

- Perception of a chaotic, luck-festival with a bit of randomness. Chaotic, it can be. But I think experience flattens this some.

- Availability again. Yeah...

RATING: 4
Very unintuitive game at first.

Mechanics is quite fresh, but it doesn't matter.

There are serious flaws in the design:
- cards enourage you to create many interesting combos, but the game is too short make more than 1-2 of them.  And the rest is just loading the goods into the treasury.  Nothing more in the game...  Despite the promise, the game is one-dimensional...
- interlocking abilities/combos are often complicated making it very difficult to track what's going on at others' play areas
- siginificant downtime
[because of the need to follow others' complicated combinations and the general downtime, max. 3-player game is sensible]
- some players can get better cards/buildings than others and thus they will be impossible to beat

I'm not a combo-fan, but even if I was and all above weaknesses weren't true, I'd be actively avoiding the game.  It just doesn't excite me in the slighest degree.  When playing it I'm deadly bored and only pray for others to make their moves fast so that we can finish the game ASAP.

Maybe it's not as bad game as I picture it.  Maybe it has decent mechanics.  Maybe it has appeal for many, but I'm surely not one of them.  I'm strongly repelled by the game after 3 plays.  It's totally not for me.

RATING: 9
A wilder version of San Juan / Race for the Galaxy.  Clearly not as tightly designed as either of those, but it places a focus on having a good time and succeeds there nicely.  The game starts slowly, and then as buildings are completed and the clientele accumulate it explodes into a combo-fest.  In some games that would be a bad thing, but that seems to be the point of GtR.

Out of two friends who like Race as much as I do, one of them loves GtR and the other hates it.  I think that GtR is great.  It's an economic snowball engine on meth, with some solid hand-management and depth added in.  It's not supposed to be a "this is serious business" game.  The attitudes of the players are important to enjoying this.

Most of my plays have been with 2.  I've played it once with 5, and it was great.  The Legionary role comes into its own with that many people.  A client or two and a Bridge, and suddenly that role can become a wrecking ball.

RATING: 7.5
2012-02-09

Initial Rating: 7.0 (November 2010)

This game has been growing on me, my second favorite card game (after RFTG), the mechanics can be hard to teach but the game is really simple and it is an strategic/tactic gem. I think I am in the minority here but I really like the original artwork, and dislike the Black Box one. The good thing about Glory to Rome is the great number of aspects that play very well together, you have role selection, lots of player interactions, some luck, card combos, hard decisions (do I lead this role, build this building or use it as materiel) among others. All of this completes a very good and complex game which is why it is very challenging to do well. I totally recommend it.

My only complaint (although a very minor one) is the game box, I have seen many cards get damaged during shipping due to the box.

Bottom line, Glory to Rome is a gem, but you need to give it the chance to amaze you, you need to play this at least 5 times to really see why it shines.

RATING: 9
Card game in the same genre as San Juan and Race for the Galaxy, in that the cards have multiple uses (role selection, buildings, building materials, bankable money), and it's up to you to decide which cards to play in which roles. Completed buildings give you additional powers which make the difference between winning and losing.

Game play is smoother than it at first seems. The complexity comes through players often having a lot of options from which to choose.

Rated 7.5 after 1 3-player game with all new players, suspect this could rise with further plays. 2 of the 3 players liked it (including me), the third didn't.

Production isn't of the highest quality, and the cartoony artwork suggests a lighter game than is actually the case, but it's nice to see a small outfit publishing a good game that seems to be becoming a sleeper success.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This may not be as tightly designed as SJ or RfG; but it's the most fun of the whole genre!  It feels like someone oiled up the squeaky joints on those other games-- more cards, more number of powers, more extravagant powers, (therefore, more combos), more steps to build things, more ways to use roles. "San Juan meets Magic," as one of the creators said. The cards don't break the game; rather it's a race to see who can break the game first. 
Because of its complexity (740 two-card combinations, tens of thousands of three?), GtR works even better than its cousins for 2p. (I recommend learning with 2p before attempting more.) There are no "obvious choices" like SJ. I normally don't like such complex games; but with clever design (exposing different ends of the cards under different sides of the player mats) this is really a model of elegance.
I know the art is roundly criticized; but what critics ignore is how amazingly functional it is--the bright colors work really well to visually simplify the complexity. The I.V. ed player mats are a model of elegance, telling you exactly what and where you need to do for each role. I find the cartoony art consistent with the exaggerated cartoony powers. An extravagant game needs extravagant artwork. (This is superman, not chess.) The instruction booklet is excellent too.
Biggest worry is that underneath it will turn out to be shallow, and that the strategy won't get much beyond "this combo counters this combo, how do i get it and prevent them from getting it?"  But too early to tell.

RATING: N/A
Rahdo must have
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
It is hard to assess Glory to Rome without comparing it to San Juan and Race for the Galaxy. I do enjoy the role-selection/multi-purpose card play of all these games. I did play them each in order of complexity and have been increasingly impressed with the possibilities these mechanics offer. But Glory to Rome is the first one that has truly impressed me. (RftG is impressive as well, but really the game is too short, which is why I score it a point lower.)

Rome crams all sorts of uses into a single card - roles, clients, foundations, materials, influence, special abilities. The victory conditions ensure a longer game than Race, which has a huge effect on the quality of play. In Race, you pretty much have to pick a strategy early and play it out. If you try to shift gears partway through, you're done. In Rome, there is more time to assess your strategy and shift gears if it isn't working, or react to what other players are doing - all of which makes for a more thoughtful game. I like that the player who invests in clients is the one who gets the extra actions, and you don't get bonuses for simply being the leader. Being able to select the role is your bonus, plus in some cases order of play is an advantage as well. The fact that the discard pile ("the pool") is actively in play is a fantastic innovation. I think it is a VERY solid strategic card game. The design is a bit garish and it takes time to grok, but it's worth it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Chris Rao really hit on something when he described Glory to Rome as "more creative and less mechanical." The buildings provide some surprising and uproariously fun advantages in GtR, in contrast with games ranging from Jambo (with it's straightforward card/ware/gold equivalencies) to Race (with it's larger range of straightforward draw/min-max advantages). I'm not sure there are "balance" issues here either, as numerous personal comments attest. Rather, I think the game is designed so that most of the combination machinery can and will spin nigh-out-of-control as the endgame approaches. You can't really single out a card that is "broken" by fastidious Eurogaming standards; the whole deck is potentially "broken." Compare this to Agricola, where superb play barely nets you a decent farm, and the entire game centers around eeking out a few extra actions. In Glory to Rome, you get to run after the warm-up.

Rated a "10" just in time for the new year (2009).  

After lots of three-player games, I'm a tad bit wary of 5-player, although perhaps just with new players. I would like to play several four-player games, though. 

Edit: I rate the 5-player game a 7. A good way to spend 45 minutes, but with 5 you will not hit the full potential of the game. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Similar enough to Race for the Galaxy and San Juan to pique my interest, different enough to be worth having.  I haven't really figured this one out yet, but I like it a lot.  I'm not sure if it's deeper than RftG or just less elegant.  It's certainly deeper than SJ.  

1st Ed production values are crap, but don't let that scare you away from a great game!  I.V is better, though it's nowhere near RftG & SJ.

What really draws me to GtR is how different every game is.  After 20 or so plays, I have yet to play the same game twice.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The cute artwork initially made me think this was a light game, but then you learn it requires plenty of strategy. Once you start to understand the game it becomes a lot of fun. Your cards can be played in multiple ways. On each turn a card is played with a character that has a special action. Other players can follow with the same card, a wild card, or one of their stored matching characters. The characters on the cards allow building, attacking, storing characters, or card transfers into a stockpile, or into a vault. The buildings are built using the same character cards, now used as resources. Cards grant various special powers which are helpul to building. Buildings, cards in the vault, and other bonus determine the winner.

RATING: 8
My 1199th rated game!

I really delayed getting on board with Glory to Rome, first because of availability issues, but then because of all the talk about how complicated it was.  It turns out that (at least for me) that claim is unfounded, as it has been fairly easy to teach so far, just by reading the rules.

There's nothing really original I can say about the game.  The theme is laughably thin, completely inconsequential as far as how the game plays.  The artwork is also distracting and on the whole hurts the game.  But I appreciate the relative simplicity of the simple and the obvious potential for different types of strategy.  Sure, the luck of the draw can definitely hurt you, but that can be somewhat mitigated by special powers on the cards.  And even so, the game doesn't last too long anyway.

I do think the game ending cards are a little cheap, especially since you can end the game almost right after having started.

My main gripe with the game relates to the physical production and components.  While component issues are definitely less important than the actual game content and experience, it is definitely annoying putting the game away and the glossy cardstock is cumbersome as well.  If someone released an updated version with high quality cards and a more sensible box (without the stupid tuck boxes), with updated graphics, it would really be a winner.  That said, I'll still be playing this game and enjoying it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Strangely, Glory to Rome really scratches my Magic the Gathering itch.  It's not similar mechanically.  But the way that the buildings break the rules and the possibility of very powerful building combos make this game diverse, swingy and fun every time ... just like a good set of Magic cards.  This game is much more approachable and a lot more fun than Race for the Galaxy.  San Juan is better with 2 players or with non-gamers.  
***Edit*** I traded San Juan away.  It's an almost perfect design, but it just doesn't have enough bumpiness in the ride to make it interesting and fun in the long run.  Glory to Rome just gets better and better, though.

Update july 2015:
Finally got my second play in. And a third will probably follow soon. 

The game is not hard to play at all. the difficulty for new players are the definitions used in the game. Hand, stockpile, pool. And there is no clear reason why one would move from there playing that role besides it says so on your player aid/map.

I have to check the scroing system because I don't understand my initial comment. of five points for one card I vaulted.

RATING: 7
Very involved card game in which each card can be used several different ways.  You are seeking to build structures that will grant you special abilities, produce goods which can be stored away for additional victory points, and give you additional actions if you build your "client" base.  Its not actually all that complex, but figuring out the different building combinations and what role to pick on your turn can be a difficult decision, particularly since everyone else has the opportunity to copy your action if they have a similar role card.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[u]Comments:[/u]
When playing Glory to Rome you can definitely feel the lineage the gameplay has, sprouting out of [gameid=8217], which in turn was a sprout off of [gameid=3076]. The overall feel of the game really beefs up what [gameid=8217] has to offer, and throws in a nice dash of Carl Chudyk killer combos to boot. Even though you can feel Chudyk's inspirations throughout the game you also feel his unique stamp on the game through every one of the mechanics.

When first listening to the rules of how to play Glory to Rome your head will swim with all of the possibilities that one card could possibly be, but once you jump into the game and play a couple of rounds the gameplay is very streamlined and moves at a really nice pace throughout. 

The Black Box version of the game is simply stunning to behold, and to me represents one of the greatest achievements in modern game graphic design. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
I can't feel anything like the variety and depth of Race for the Galaxy, here (only 5-6 buildings, at the end; no thematic coherence between the cards; no brain-burning plans [because of the limited number of powers, and their relatively simple interlocking mechanisms,…]).

Less variety than Innovation (because the board situation does not change very fast), less subtle strategy than Race for the Galaxy (because the Building powers have big effects). However, juggling with the different Roles and their requirements (having a matching Material in Hand for the Legionary, playing a Role knowing it will go to the Stockpile, from where it can be used to build Buildings, etc.) make implementing plans not fully straightforward. Also, keeping in mind the interaction of all the powers in Play is a somewhat challenging: it's easy to overlook something.

I am a little disappointed by how fast a combo from an opponent can put me behind: they are hard to predict and counter.

I appreciate the simplicity of the Black Box edition: the cards are very legible.

Good: interactive, with aggressive cards that force reactions and/or defense building.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[thing=19857][/thing] was was hugely hyped after the reprint was announced, particularly as it was billed as a more interactive [thing=28143][/thing], one of our favorite games.  We tend to like these types of tableau-building games where you get to build up your area with special cards.

We got a new copy and eagerly tried it out...and it didn't quite bowl us over right off the bat.  The cartoony artwork of the IV edition wasn't a problem (we actually like the bright colors, since they helped to distinguish your opponent's cards across the table).

[thing=19857][/thing] has some interesting mechanisms, particularly the common pool cards, which results in some unique card flow.  However, we're not sure that two players is where the game shines---it seems like  it's too few players to make the pool mechanism really shine.  There's just not enough interactivity with two.  We had a game where both of us were very reluctant to discard anything to the pool, so we ended up taking the Thinking action over and over again, which made the game drawn out and boring.  Plus, the "game-breaking" card powers didn't feel all that special.  At least for two, the game felt more like a slow, grind-it-out affair until one player can break it wide open with a great combo and sprint to the end.  In this case, having more players and more chaos might benefit the game.  For now, I think we prefer the better-paced Race, although we'll have to give it a few more tries.

RATING: 8
[2009-03-18] My rating here could rise (should). Much more fun than Race For The Galaxy, much more interesting than San Juan. Great components, great artwork (thought busy). The many paths to victory ensure a nicely different game on each play.

I dislike some of the odd wordings on the cards and in the text. For example, it is not intuitively obvious to all readers just what "...as a jack" means, and especially not in all cases. What this means is that the 'object' is played as if it was a jack. "...any three Order cards of the same role (color) as a Jack" is read by some as saying that the 3 order cards must be the same color as the Jack, which makes no sense, and adds unnecessary confusion.

Too bad about the crappy plastic box which arrived in the mail open for me! ...damaging the player mats (DARN - I hate that, almost sent the game back). After some repair work the damage is hardly noticeable.

Anyway, [b]FUN[/b].

[2012-12-09] I sure am glad I got the I.V. version. We happen to like the original cartoony look, and the upgrade from the 1st edition to I.V. is great. Got the 2 added card sets from BGG's store and couldn't be happier. This game is complete for us, and we never need the ugly spartan Black Box edition. Done! And happy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The art sucks.  The art beyond sucks.  It's horrendous.  Almost to the point of being offensively bad.  Which is a real tragedy, because this is one of the greatest games I have ever played.  The originality, the strategic depth might be unparalleled.  Every card can be used 4 different ways, and each way then puts it into a different play space for future interactions.  The cardflow is so interesting and so clever.  The building's powers vary from weak and mildly interesting (on their own) to "did I read that right? Can I really do that??" (hint: yes you can).  The game is intentionally "broken," so that it is a race to break it first with an all-powerful ridiculous over-the-top combo of powers, including a few of those aforementioned "weak" ones, which when combined with the right things only multiply the power of others and launch them into the stratosphere.  Tons of player interaction, most of it indirect (a few attacky things do exist). Every play effects the other players, every choice matters.  The game is SO SO SO SO good.  So good.  Fantastic 2 players.  Fantastic with more as well.  Everyone does something on each turn, so the game never drags, even when players sit there trying to decide what to do (because chances are you have a lot to think about as well).

Alas, due to the art, most people will never even give it a try.  I will say, that while very much like a slap in the face, the art fades into the background when you play.  Most cards are stacked in various ways, and you're so focused on the color and text, and you almost don't notice how ugly it is.

A fancy kickstarter alternative art in minimalist style version does exist, although it was $100 at the time and was a limited print run, so... yeah.

RATING: 7
The chatter on BGG over the new edition of this game brought it back to my attention and I considered whether I would spring for a copy of the new look version. But after consultation with my wife, I found she preferred the look of the already available version - the clarity of which color cards are which in particular was mentioned. I wasn't too sure about the cartoony art and the possible similarities with Race for the Galaxy, but enough Geeks here praised it that I put some of my birthday money toward a copy.

I can safely say I haven't regretted it. There is certainly room in a collection for both Race and G2R, with Glory to Rom providing a wilder experience, the card combinations sometimes threatening to shut down the game. The encouragement of the publishers to go for it with the combos is entirely in tune with this feeling, even as it feels a bit wrong that these things are so powerful. My feeling is that Race is a better design, but I am enjoying the attempts that I have made so far to grab the reins of this game to make it go where I want, but mostly it takes me and I just hang on.

RATING: 10
High level of player interaction, difficult decisions for how to use one's cards most advantageously, engine building, a potentially high screwage factor, and creative, crazy combos.  Pure fun with the right group.  Best with 3-5 players. RATING: 10
This is a tableau building game where cards have multiple uses.  The game has two versions, one with cartoonish art and the other with "serious" art.  It is a brilliant game and with many strategic choices and many paths to victory.  I like the Republic variant a little better than the original game.  It plays differently depending on the number of players but it is a lot of fun. 

Many folks consider it heavy but it is really a medium-weight game.  

Like most card games, the better you know the cards and combinations the stronger you will play.   

You can play the game with the family but you need to take your time teaching and play the simple game at first may be worthwhile.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A lot more going on here than in San Juan or Race for the Galaxy, which are easy comparisons.  40 buildings to learn and figure out interactions.  Plays longer than RftG, which is both good and bad.  I have had the same concerns as others about balance and length of play, but once you play a few times and learn the strategies and counters to them, it balances out and play time speeds up.  This is an hour or so game if you are playing it right.  Although easily overlooked, GtR IV edition should win an award for the most superfluous pieces in the plastic bonus chips.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A fun card game, if a little chaotic. However, it's description as a "strategic" card game is a lie. There's no strategy here at all. You make the best use of each hand of cards as you get them, then get a new one and work with that. It's all tactical, as there's no way to control or predict what cards you'll get in the future, and the variety of effects is so varied that you can't plan for any of them. There's also only one way to win, apart from some crazy cards that offer a separate win condition, if things happen to fall right.

RATING: 7.5
Surprisingly good game, although the artwork of the Italian version could suggest a childish target. 
For those who are familiar with San Juan, this game is a deeper and more complex version of it. Some gimmicks really shine, like the "hiring" system, and there are so many different buildings which provide a plenty of combos. 
Paths to victory are several, due expecially to some "instant win" possibilities... which generally I don't like but in this game everything is counterable and beatable if you choose well your timing; plus, it adds some tension and the necessity to look carefully at other players' boards.
In conclusion, this is really a "tier 1" card game but unfortunately I find the artwork really annoying.

RATING: 7
Turning a stack of innocent cards into a serious brainburner seems to be a specialty of Carl Chudyk, but getting acquainted with this earlier effort after you already know and love Innovation is a bit of a letdown. Not because the games are too similar - the overlap of ideas is minimal, actually, apart from riding along with the actions of other players - but more because Glory to Rome feels less developed, at least on my first play.

It’s hard to pinpoint what contributed to this, and it certainly is good enough to make me try again in spite of being a bit underwhelmed, but what struck me as the most problematic thing is scaling. We were playing with five players, and the game kind of ended before it started because the draw deck was depleted. There was no real specialization of strategies because no one had more than three clientele cards, which seemed such a potentially fun thing to develop. More problematically, I won the game only due to two bonus VP cards, which I got with exactly two cards in the vault - the other two players who were using Merchants managed to exactly neutralize each other. Those bonus VPs were 6 of my 16 points, and that just feels wrong for so little effort. It probably balances better when playing with fewer folks, but will be even worse with six.

The art does not help, less due to its garishness, but more because the design obfuscates the game mechanics instead of supporting them. Hopefully I can try the graphic redesign for my next play to find out how much of a difference it makes.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Now this is a game I'll never turn down the chance to play. There's nothing like stringing together that perfect set of building combos to take you to victory. After a few plays, you'll get a hang of what most of the buildings do and you can start making your bomb to blow this game wide open.

Opposite of that, there are counters to the big bad bomb combos, there are buildings and other conditions that can end the game prematurely, and this works as a perfect defense against someone trying to tech hard.

The mechanics are simple and intuitive. As you get the hang of it, everything fits into place. The player mats are clear for any beginners learning the game. The mechanics also ensure that no one is really ever sitting and doing nothing. When it isn't your turn, you usually have at least two actions to choose from.

In the end, you can play a civil game, leaving your opponents alone and what not, or you can go for their jugular. No matter the playstyle you like, this game is plain good fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I LOVE this game! It just feels so fresh, and it seems infinitely repayable. I'm not a fan of San Juan (or Puerto Rico for that matter), I can't get myself to play Race for the Galaxy, and because of that, I was hesitant to pick this one up. I'm so glad I did! The gameplay is dynamic without being overwhelming. The components are quite nice (Black Box version) and I love the minimalistic art style. It's also worth mentioning that there is a TON of game in a fairly small box. If there is a game on my shelf that takes up a lot of space, I need a good reason to keep it there. With Glory to Rome, I don't have to make that distinction. However, if I did, I wouldn't mind if this was the size of Twilight Imperium 3rd Edition or a Carcassonne Big Box. I don't think everyone will like this game, mainly because, in my opinion, many won't explore the game sufficiently (it can be somewhat overwhelming your first time). Regardless of this, I think Glory to Rome deserves a spot on every serious gamer's shelf. I paid over $100 for my copy, and would have paid twice that in hindsight. Nevertheless, I hope that the publisher re-releases this gem!

Update 8/22/15: 

Played this again with my wife tonight. It's such a cool game. I just love the feel of Glory to Rome. There's really nothing else quite like it. I got massacred by my wife through unlucky card draw. There is really nothing in the game to prevent bad luck or a catch-up mechanism for that matter. It is sometimes painfully obvious that you are going to lose, and it wasn't necessarily any thing you did wrong, just bad luck. Therefore, there's a high degree of randomness in GTR. Interestingly, it doesn't really bother me. I LOVE this game, and it will remain in my top 10.

- - -
Hm, hard to rate this one after two plays. My first game was approx 90 mins and the second game slightly longer. That seemed about right though there was some AP in one session. At 90 mins I´ll be happy to play this any time. If it runs longer, not so sure.

I really like the mechanisms here. Actually, I think they are brilliant. Some buildings I´m not so sure about. Coliseum can cause some hard feelings. I´m giving this a 9, for now. Next few sessions will tell if that should be an 8.

RATING: 9
What I like:
- A good amount of player interaction with legionary and following with clientele.
- Building up your clientele to be more efficient at actions
- Large variety of building powers make each game different, and it's fun to think about how to combine those powers
- Low player downtime due to following roles

What I don't like:
- Sometimes you can get lucky drawing the perfect combo of crazy buildings, as well as luck in drawing the materials you need to finish those buildings
- It is incredibly hard to get a merchant into the clientele unless you have a special building power or if the person right before you uses the merchant card.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Bought on playbazar.it 8/3/16.  The shipping cost is ridiculous, but Mary prefers the Italian art.  It will also help us in learning Italian.

---

The game starts out slow, but quickly snowballs.  The combinations possible in this game often seem gamebreaking, which often times create seriously epic turns.  And yet, the game still feels balanced.  Great replayability due to the angst of multi-use cards.

The Italian version is turning out to be a bit more work than we thought.  I don't mind the Italian so much, but the Camp board is way too big.  The cards themselves are also fairly large.  Condensing all of these can really go a long way towards saving table space.

Definite runaway leader problem, which makes it hard to get people to play.

RATING: 8
Call me shallow, but I refused to even touch the game with its original artwork. Wouldn't eat Beluga caviar from a used handkerchief either, so yes, I'm picky. Fortunately with the new edition boom with several different artworks finally let me take a closer look, and unsurprisingly I like it. As a late arrival with heavy Race for the Galaxy background, I can't avoid measuring GtR to Rftg. 

I'm used to Race's tidiness, so the first thing I noticed is the messy way Rome handles both the gameflow and the tableau space. For the first few times it's quite a task to track what clients/resources you have, what bonuses your buildings provide, how could you produce goods to the pool, or whose turn is it anyway? I'd say it has a steeper learning curve than RftG, but after you got used to the system it's fine. Seemingly there are more strategy in the game than base Race, there are more colorful combos to discover. I wouldn't say Rome is deeper regarding strategic choices, more spread-out rather. A fine game, certainly worth a try to anyone who enjoyed San Juan or Race for the Galaxy.

RATING: 7
Having never really liked the simplicity of San Juan and having grown tired of Race for the Galaxy, Glory to Rome scratches the perfect itch for a complex, strategic card game.  I like how each of the cards serve multiple roles, but also maintain their value in every situation.  The cards with the most helpful building powers would also be worth the most if you vaulted them instead and would provide the most powerful actions and allies if used as such.  Plus, any actions you choose to take get dropped into the general pool for others to snag and use to their own advantage.  There's a constant struggle for how to best use the cards in your hand, which makes the gameplay meaningful, exciting, and enjoyable.

RATING: 8.5
Terrific multi-user card game.  Among the best in class.  Let's call this Race for the Galaxy's unruly older brother.  If Race is a "Euro" than GtR is it's "Amerithrash" shadow twin.

This can be tough for new players, and teaching the game requires skill or else players who are willing to just dive in.  There is a lot to chew on here.  The game can be swingy and luck can play a large role from time to time, but overall smart play outweighs luck.  Crazy combos are part of the design.

I always have a great time playing this, and after many plays, I've raised my rating.

RATING: 7
San Juan look-alike. Definitely deeper than San Juan, but not necessarily better -- the luck of the draw can be crippling (when you need one specific resource to complete a building but just can't get it - granted there are some mitigating actions you can take), and the insane variety of buildings means that you might just not draw that one that you need to complete your combo. However, there is a lot of thinking going on, definitely many different ways to go about winning,and overall much meatier feel to the game. It is overly complex to grok at first and takes a number of turns to really understand what is going on (which can be very frustrating for beginners). 
I find Race for the Galaxy to be a better implementation of the same overall concept.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
It took me 3/4 of a game to understand its rhythm and how the various actions interact with each other.  What I found was a game with a large variety of strategies and tactical decisions throughout.  In many respects it's a race game and although one can build up to some really powerful combos the game may be over before you have a chance to convert the fruit of your labors to victory points.  This is why the game is compared to Race to the Galaxy.  

The cards are very cleverly designed in that they have multiple functions depending on how/where they are used: a building material, a power, VPs, influence points and an action selection power.  With a handful of these cards and more available within the deck and pool it can be very overwhelming at first but it all starts to click by the end of your first game and the variety of options should ensure that each game is a different experience.

RATING: 10
Best w/3-4, 2-5:

Also own the Black Box Edition

Imagine if Puerto Rico and Cosmic Encounter had a baby which they named it Glory to Rome.  GtR Cons:  Kind of a hodge podge of rules, it's difficult to teach, it usually takes the better part of your first game to get a handle on the rules and strategy, and so it's a gamer's game.  Pros:  Somehow it all works...you are actively engaged on every players turn, all of the cards are overpowered so it balances somewhat, it's got some back and forth (legionnaire), it's got engine building in a sense, you are racing to complete your buildings so there is tension, depending on what you build every game feels different (variable player powers).  My only regret is not being able to get this to the table more often.

RATING: 7.5
Finally got to play this after waiting about 2 years.  I love it, probably like it better than Race for the Galaxy.

However, I played it first with a person who's probably played a dozen or more games of it, and so he'd memorized many of the cards and learned many possible combos.  So, I was taken aback at the game's quick end both times, as he played cards to end the game massively earlier than expected (but clearly within the rules).  

I'm not sure I like the early-end possibilities included in the game (especially since I'm not sure I want to have to memorize all possible combos to watch out for them), but I'm interested to see how it plays out.

If it weren't for the early-victory combos, this would be a 9; as it is, it's a 7.5 until I play it more.

RATING: 9.15

The art is garbage, but it adds to the charm, honestly.

RATING: 8
The rulebook for this game is incredible and should be an example to all other game publishers. There is an example for every card! 

Catacombs and Forums are the most important buildings. Forums let you win the game immediately (by having one client of each type) and Catacombs let you steal a victory through VPs by forcing the end of the game. I believe these two building types are the main focus of the
game as they give you control on when it will end IMMEDIATELY.

This game definitely deserves a replay and I usually don't like VP engine type games. I guess it's because this game actually has player interaction and variable end conditions!

RATING: 7
Ender is right: [thread=371582]this is the game Race wanted to be[/thread]. The game plays differently each time and demands constant player interaction. Takes longer than quickies like Dominion, but you don't lose time shuffling cards.

After almost 40 plays, I have to admit this has gotten a little old. I still won't turn down a game, am glad to have it in my collection, and enjoy it when I play it, but I'm less inclined to suggest it. I also have almost no interest in teaching it, as the explanation takes [i]forever[/i], new players are invariably lost no matter how well it's taught, and I feel obliged to play the inferior Republic version. Thus, in specific circumstances, this is an 8, but most of the time it's a 6, so I've split the difference for my current rating.

RATING: 7
In der kleinen Schachtel von Ruhm für Rom steckt eine ganze menge Spiel drin. Außerdem ist Ruhm für Rom kein Leichtgewicht, sondern bietet durchaus komplexe Regeln. Mittels Karten versuchen die Spieler die Stadt Rom wieder aufzubauen, die nach dem großen Feuer 64 n.Chr. stark verwüstet wurde. Die Karten können dabi auf unterschiedliche Arten genutzt werden, z.b. um Ressourcen zu bekommen, Gebäude zu bauen oder seine eigene Schatzkammer zu füllen. Man muss sich als Spieler immer entscheiden, wie man seine Karten am sinnvollsten nutzt. Der Einstieg in Ruhm für Rom ist nicht ganz einfach, danach entfaltet das Spiel aber sein volles Potential. Für Strategen und Planer absolut empfehlenswert!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In this Roman themed card game, each card has three things it can represent: it can be a client (architect, crafstman, merchant, legionary, laborer, or patron), it can be a building material (rubble, wood, concrete, brick, stone or marble) or it can be a building. On a player's turn to be leader, they play a card out of their hand to do that client's ability (e.g., play an architect to start a building or get material for a building). Other players can follow suit to get the same ability, then the next player gets to be leader. Wild cards known as "jacks" allow one to follow suit if they do not have the card. 

Each player has a player mat, where cards are stored. Depending where the card is stored, it is a client (gives further actions if you or an opponent choose that action), or it is a building material in "stockpile" area, or it counts as VPs in the vault. 

This is a fun game, with many interesting card combinations. I want to play this at least 10 more times to get the feel of it. Most of the learning curve is in the first game, then you can start exploring strategies, such as having an early merchant to earn VPs in your vault, or other clients. This game has a lot of potential to be good. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
My #1 favorite game!

I love it for the fact that there's no set-ways of playing it. The combos those building's abilities can give are endless. Being creative both strategically tactically would likely to award you with more wins, that's the best thing I like about this game. Once I didn't play to win (cuz my friend had lost a few times straight so I tried to go easy,) I still had fun just building whatever buildings come in handy and hire whoever that's available. (On top of that, I still ended up winning..) 

Just build and hire first then think about what to do with them next! You might just come up with new ways of playing it. 

This game is like a bag of pleasant surprises for me.

Pros:
1. Deep in strategy.
2. No optimal/sure-win strategy.
3. High replay value.
4. Great player interaction.
5. Lots of different combos to be discovered.
6. Feel differently each time you play.
7. Helluva FUN!

Cons:
1. Below par art (I don't give a damn~)
2. Bad packaging (But who gives damn!)
3. Okay, it's not always THAT fun. Could be boring sometimes especially when one's getting an extremely poor card draw, or an extremely lucky card draw. BUT only sometimes!

Note:
GF also likes this game! Wuuhaaaa~~~

RATING: N/A
規則:
*羅馬需求卡放中間，訂單卡洗勻蓋著放，百搭牌放一旁，每個顏色建築卡分類洗勻開人數張數，剩下的放一旁
*每人拿一個個人圖板，每人抽五張訂單卡，為每個人在中央開一張訂單卡，字母靠前的起始，平手再開，起始拿領袖卡，所有訂單卡在中央形成牌池
*遊戲輪流進行，每個玩家回合行動二選一，直到結束條件一發生馬上結束
>選擇思考  可抽一張百搭或是首牌補到上限(通常五張)，或是手牌到上限時抽一張
>出牌  出一張牌使用左邊的腳色能力行動，此時所有其他玩家都可選擇跟出或是選擇思考(同上)，之後從領袖玩家開始順時針每人可執行此腳色行動，次數等於出的牌加上他的圖版左邊工人數，行動完後出的訂單卡都移到牌池，領袖卡左傳
*百搭卡可當任意領袖卡出，之後放回對應牌庫，任意兩張一樣顏色的訂單卡也可當任意腳色卡出，也可執行原本腳色卡行動變兩次
*腳色功能如下
>紫色雇用工人  拿一張牌池的牌差到圖板左側只露出左邊腳色字樣，腳色上限等於圖板上方影響力數
>黃色拿資源 拿一張牌池的牌塞到圖板下方當作資源，資源上限等於圖板上方影響力數
>灰色建築師  可出一張手牌放到面前並拿對應顏色的開的建築卡放到下方當基座，或是把一張圖版下方對應顏色資源移到有基座的牌下
>綠色工匠 可出一張手牌放到面前並拿對應顏色的開的建築卡放到下方當基座，或是把一張對應顏色的手牌當作資源移到有基座的牌下
*如果對應顏色的基座沒有就要使用兩個同色行動來使用蓋著的牌當作基座，同名字建築不能再蓋，當一個建築物下方牌數等於右上圖案數就完成，將基座卡翻面差到圖板上方，資源繼續在卡牌下
>紅色需求資源 展示一張牌，左右手玩家開牌池都拿一張對應顏色牌當作資源塞到你的圖版下方，執行多次時，要一次展示所有需求資源(展示不夠多就不能執行)
>藍色賣牌 移動下方資源區一張牌到圖板右方蓋著，上限等於你的影響力數
*遊戲在牌庫抽完，最後一個底座被拿走(蓋建築不會被蓋好)，或是特殊牌蓋出，或是其他人投降，則遊戲馬上結束，除了特殊建築或投降，每個影響力一分，每張賣出的牌拿上下方物品數分數，每個顏色賣出物品最多的額外拿三分

RATING: 6
Seems like San Juan only better since there are more strategies you can try. It can get very chaotic in the late game as everything spirals out of control until eventually the game terminates.

The game is brimming with 'overpowered' combos waiting to be found - anywhere else they'd break the game, but here it doesn't matter because everyone can make a 'broken' combo, so it sort of balances out...maybe... 

I've decided I prefer Race (20 mins) to Glory to Rome (c.60 mins) due to play time. Puerto Rico is preferable if you have 60 mins.

Bought Jan/Feb 2009, sold summer 2010 whilst OOP

RATING: 10
This is one of my stranded-on-an-island games !!

Excellent Fun Refreshing Variable-Phase Order Card-Management Game !! Wonderful feel to the strange gameplay. Humorous. Interesting card combo potentials. Very different in feel than other role selection card games, IMO. Thank you, Lee family for teaching us this game !!

I really enjoy the famous quotes on each card, and I don't mind the artwork and colorful graphics of the pre-Black Box editions. I think they add to the humor of the wild combos, and to the ensuing chaos. The impressive graphics of the Black Box might make the game a little dry for me.

This game deserves to be allowed for another publisher to reprint this game properly. To whom it may concern, please let "Glory to Rome" go so it can live.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
The build of the game is... well, it's pretty piss poor. Some of the cards are misprinted, the stock on the "camp" mats is too flimsy and lightweight, the instructions are poorly written and confusing and the box can only be described as disposable. I enjoyed the game mechanic itself, but found that the design of the cards was too busy and distracting, all the more so when compared to this game's nearest neighbor, Race To The Galaxy, which seems to put more information on the cards with less text, nicer fonts, much easier-on-the-eyes art and more intuitive layout. It's a fine game when you get past all that, but the getting-past-all-that poses as much of a challenge as any opponent you'd face.

Overall, the game is badly in need of a buff-up and cosmetic redesign. So much so that, while playing, my mind wandered into thinking about doing it myself. Not bad at all, but clearly the work of guys who care more about the game they've come up with and much less about the medium itself. Considering how competitive the market is and how many incredibly rendered games came out this year, it's barely passable.

RATING: 7
This card game has the San Juan/Race for the Galaxy thing going where someone chooses a role, and then you have to make the best use out of it.  That's where the comparison ends, though.  Cards in the game can be used as roles you initiate, permanent roles for when they are initiated, buildings that give you advantages and points, materials for those buildings, or even materials that just give you points.  There's a definite flow that's pretty difficult to wrap your head around the first couple of times playing, but once you figure it out, it's a good strategic game.

(3 plays)

RATING: 8
A strategy packed card game. Each card has multiple uses and every turn requires trade off decisions. A geek game and requires 2 "training" games just to get a hang of the mechanics and to develop a preliminary strategy. 

The less said about game art, the better. For a game that has such a strong reputation and fan following among gamers who like strategy games, the game art is just atrocious and makes you feel like it is a children's game. But don't judge a game by its art. 

Finding partners who can understand how to play and then devise strategies to play it well isn't the easiest thing given its learning curve in that each card can play several roles - possible building, role, or material. Additionally, there is some luck involved in the cards drawn - sometimes, you just won't get powerful enough buildings or those that pair well with other buildings you have.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I tend to think of Glory to Rome as a trick taking game  though no tricks are ever taken.  On a turn, a player plays and action card.  The other players can choose to also perform that action by following suit with a card of their own.

Actions allow a player to get resources, build buildings and "ship" resources for points.  The cards are multipurpose acting as actions, buildings, resources and points.  The thing that takes Glory to Rome and shoots it into the stratosphere relative to other games of its ilk is the variety and extreme nature of the special powers the buildings provide.

The building powers makes each game a wildly careening affair.  In isolation each card may appear completely broken.  When they are all combined the game blows up.  It's crazy and incredibly fun responding to the buildings players have built and the clients they have managed to acquire.  That's not to say the game is random or chaotic.  But you definitely want to hang on to your seats.  And if you lose your momentum in the game it's possible to be absolutely savaged by the other players.

This game is the answer to the accusations that efficiency engine games are multi-player solitaire.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Very unique and insanely addictive.  Better with more players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Jan 2012: Down to 4. I don't particularly like "tableau building" card drafting/economic engine games.

2011-01-05: Tentative 7 after one play with only half the deck. I'm not a fan at all in non-collectible CCGs / VP engine games, so the rating for this game is likely to go down.

Pros

* In relation to Race for the Galaxy and San Juan, much more elegant ruleset. No bizarre icons and much easier to understand game structure than either RftG or SJ.

* It's a typical VP engine game as you build buildings that give you special powers, which makes you get VPs faster. Unlike VP engine games in which you don't have much of a chance to get to use the uber-powerful buildings, GtR allows you to build (and eventually use) any building you want right from the start of the game.

* The beginner game of removing half of the cards makes GtR a pretty good non-gamer game.

Cons

* Really, really, really fiddly, especially compared to RftG and SJ. Any game that involves tucking cards underneath other cards will lead to cards constantly being shifted out of place and out of sight.

RATING: 9.25
After the first two plays of the Black Box edition: The challenge with this game was where to start explaining it to new players. If you don't have a plan, you can easily lose people before you get to a point where you can start playing. Although the rules say not to, we just started playing. Made a couple of rules discoveries during the first game, but we all really liked it and we played it again right away. I'm ready to play again, anytime, and I want to teach it to the Friday night gamers, because I think they will really dig it.

Advantages of this edition over the I.V edition: FAR superior packaging (box, insert), higher quality cards (card art and card finish), player boards have more information, rules are a little cleaner. This newer Black Box edition also includes the Republic expansion, which was made available separately for the first and I.V editions. There is debate as to whether the card art, which is drastically different, is an improvement over the campier earlier editions. Personally, I think it is. It's clearer for game play, I would argue, and better matches the tone of the game than the earlier cartoony art.

One of the best games I've played that uses just cards.

RATING: 9
Rating of 9 after first play.  I had always heard GtR was a good game for those that liked RftG - I would agree.  They use somewhat similar mechanics.

I also liked that the designers tried to tie the abilities of the building to the name of the building.  Theme is big with me, and I appreciated the effort in making the abilities "match up" with the name.  (I laughed out loud at latrine - juvenile yes, but still funny and clever)

Great game!

RATING: 6.35
Each card has several functions badly layed out, the use of them is counter-intuitive, the game suffers from certain escalation effects often beyond an individuals controlthat can be easily triggered by a poor player and the art is terrible. 

Having said that Glory to Rome is actually quite a good game. You move cards from central areas to hands to buildings to score points. These points feed-back into your play to increase what you can do. The central mechanic is that when a player takes an action every one else can follow that action, often taking the same action as the active player several times. Which provides an interesting set of challenges.

On the other hand it does feel like a game that really needs its second edition to really find its balance.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I got this game way back in 2011 as a Christmas present (the first Christmas after my wife and I got into modern boardgames). At that time I preferred games with simple rules (although I did love card games, and I knew this one was highly regarded), and I struggled with this at first - and, while I persevered, it soon became clear that most of my main game group didn't care for the game. However, I have managed to play it quite frequently since 2013 or 2014 (with a slightly different, although overlapping, group - helped by its relatively quick play time and the fact that the much-derided clamshell packaging does at least make it easy to transport along with other games), and my opinion of the game has gone up. There is a lot to think about in terms of how to use each card in your hand (as a role to lead or follow with, as a building, or as a building material for the craftsman action), and you need to think about what you put into the pool and how to best organise your leading, following and thinking in order to get the most out of everyone's actions. And that's before we even get to the real heart of the game - getting combinations of buildings which allow you to perform insanely effective chains of actions on a turn. Like many games, this one starts slowly and ramps up, but I've not played any other game where the final result of this ramping up can be quite so insane.

Perhaps this would be higher than an 8 if I played it more often, especially with players who all knew the game well. For now I don't feel I can rate it higher - and, while it's very interesting, it's not my favourite card game, I prefer both Dominion and Race for the Galaxy, which also offer great depth but have even more variety and  much simpler rules, and play quicker as well. (It's probably not even my favourite Carl Chudyk game - I usually prefer Innovation to this, although that to me is a 2p game while GtR is much much better with 3+)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Ok, this may be cult of the new on my part, but this game appears to hit all my hot buttons. It's short, but not too short (abt 1hr). It's got very little setup time and it's very portable. It scales wonderfully from 2-5 players without losing strategic depth with fewer players or excess player downtime with more players. Just the right mixture of luck:strategy for me. There's some randomness to add excitement and (healthy) bit of luck, but strategy will always trump luck in this game. The strategic depth is awesome...many many many paths to victory and every game feels different. I love economic engine games and this one hits it out of the park without feeling overly repetitive (I'm looking at you powergrid). Unlike RfTG or San Juan, the interaction between players is much much higher...there's more going on between players here than just trying to guess what role they will take and mooching off it/screwing the guy to your left. Because the cards you discard go into the community pot, you have to be very careful and observant of what's being thrown away. No so-called "multi-player solitaire" going on in this game, no no. I love card games where cards serve multiple purposes because it inherently means tough decisions...do I play this card for the role it brings? Do i use it as the building material it is?

The box it comes in is a joke, and some will complain about the artwork...I actually like the artwork so no complaints on components.

LOVE IT LOVE IT LOVE IT!

EDIT - this has dropped 2 points since I last edited this. Who's to blame? Ohhh this evil little card game called "7 Wonders", that's who. It shows the flaws of GtR bright and clear. GtR is still an awesome game, but a little chaotic IMHO now that I've played it more extensively and the game has a tendency to *not end* sometimes. The passing of your discards into a common pool makes the interaction interesting in GtR, but this is put on steroids with 7 Wonders where you pass you entire unplayed hand to your neighbor.

RATING: 8
22-01-2014. Rated after 2 2p games. Very interesting card-game. Each card has many different functions. Each card can be used as a role —that gives you a special action—, a building —that gives you special abilities—, victory points —when stored in the vault— and lastly as a resource. Cards can be added to your vault, patrons, influence and storage.

When you take actions with your role card, you're allowed to take cards from the pool as many times as you have the role card in your patron pool.. 

This is a beautiful card game. It's complex, you have so many degrees of freedom and options to think. Fantastic. One of my favorite card games.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Black Box Edition
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
----------

I LOVE this unique gem of a game.  I love the player interaction, the role selection, the role leaching, the rewards from completed buildings, and the multiple paths to victory, the insane benefits of strong synergies.  Synergy, ah yes, the name of the game.  A name that makes this card game so addictive.

BELIEVE THE HYPE.  This is a great game, and I whole-heartedly recommend it.  Luck is mitigated since there are multiple copies of each card, so unlike RftG, you don't feel like you are hopelessly mining the deck for "that ONE card" to pull your strategy together.  

Here's a little secret of mine that tends to work well:  if you find a highly rated game with sub-par components... GET IT.  Good components tend to have a strong influence on game ratings .... but you know you have a winner when the game is butt ugly, but people still rave about it because the mechanics shine through.  GtR is that type of game.  

A caveat for the potential buyers:  I thought this game was going to be deeper than it is.  There are some good decisions to be made, but similar games, such as RftG and Innovation, provide much deeper gaming experiences.  

This is my #6 game.

RATING: 9

Kind of a modern classic and with good reason. The multi-purpose cards, the unique action-following mechanism and variety of scoring paths available make it a fun and highly replayable game. Just give it a couple of tries before you write it off as incomprehensible...

RATING: 9
I'm a fan of tactical card games, and Glory To Rome is one of my A-List. Set beside RftG, it's the second half of the dyad of brilliant card games which I'll gladly play again and again and are the reason I mildly prefer card games to board games. 

The art-work is inescapable when discussing this game but my view tends to be: the art's cartoony, so what? I don't really care - any art-work is fine by me, and if you don't like it, just ignore it, and the game is fine.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Visual Appeal: (1)
Man oh man, I know everyone says it but the original printing of this game is just plain bad. The box is not attractive or even useful since it pops open without a rubber band. The only thing the cards have going for them over the new Black Box edition (That I stupidly didn't shell out for on Kickstarter) is that they are very legible.

Components: (2)
Not the best quality cards, and I highly recommend sleeving. Although this creates a massive draw pile, it is worth it to preserve the cards. As I mentioned above, the cards are very easy to read due to contrast/color even with the large amount of information they convey. The play mats are a good idea but way too small. If the game had a proper box, maybe they could have made larger mats too. I have a side project planned to create my own new mats/box for this game.

Theme: (3)
There's a back story to the game. I think it's something about rebuilding Rome after a massive fire...anyway it doesn't matter. The game is about card flow and hand management. There are some cool times where the theme peeks through and that is to the great credit of the designer Carl Chudyk. I feel like he did a better job here than in "Innovation". For example, the Vomitorium allows you to "vomit" cards into the pool. I am impressed that he was able to attach so many game actions to the historical function of the buildings.

Learning: (4)
This game is really easy to learn and hard to master. More than any card game in my collection (except maybe Race for the Galaxy) I think you must learn to read your opponents and play the strategies that present themselves. It is really easy to get stuck in a position as a new player where you want to do one thing, but the resources just aren't there to do it. I make sure that part of my introduction of the game is a reminder not to force something that isn't going to work right away. Due to the high number of duplicate cards though, long term strategies are possible to execute.

Gameplay: (5)
This is another game with a lot of screw you. There are plenty of opportunities to take resources that your opponents need and laugh maniacally as they are unable to finish structures or follow your actions. I like it a lot. 

Overall Fun: (5)
What this game lacks in appearance, it makes up for in interesting game play. Just the right amount of tension and interaction. The only one card that I don't like is the Forum. It can end games shockingly fast if it goes unchecked and it feels really unsatisfying. I want to use the Forum Romanum from the expansion when I get my hands on it. I usually play 2 player and even my friends who enjoy heavier games usually will play 1 or 2 rounds of this with me happily. This is my second favorite card game. after "Innovation."

RATING: 9
2013: Definitely my favorite non-collectible card game. As all card games, it's much more tactical than strategical and involves building a good combo before anyone else. Still, when you decide on playing some key cards, you basically define your strategy for the game. It offers much more interaction - both direct and indirect - than Race for the Galaxy and is [b]much[/b] more controllable than Innovation. The only flaw (again, quite typical to card games) is that it's not as accessible as I would like. There's text on all the cards and on the first and second play you'll need time to read and digest it to make informed decisions, leading to slow play with new players.

2016: Upping this to a 9 but I should really finally give it a tenner and get over it - I can't see ever deciding I don't want to play it anymore. With dozens of plays behind, I really appreciate how subtle and not at all chaotic it becomes with experience. It's fun how it forces you to adapt and depart from favourite strategies and becomes about intuitive assessment on whose combo will win the race and whether you should continue racing ot switch over and start pulling the game in another direction. I think that it belongs on any shortlist of greatest timeless classics.

I probably prefer Race for the Galaxy with 2, but this is the better for more players.

RATING: 7
Recently increased my rating. With further play this has not only held up well, but allowed focus to be switched from grappling with rules to grappling with devilish plans and tricky moves. I'm even enjoying it with a full compliment of five. May its visits to the table be frequent and fun.

I think three might be the right number with this game - any more and there's a little too information to keep track of. Kind of odd card game where despite initial appearance that there's a lot going on it turns out there isn't much going on at all. Limited opportunity to discard and the weak theme causes me to feel a little let down, but all in all it IS a good game. The game is really quite simple and I was a little disappointed to see that there's really only two main ways of scoring points. Most building effort seems to be around buildings that allow you to either increase the size of your vault or improve the ease of placing material inside your vault. It's not terrible, but it doesn't seem like I have the control that I have in San Juan or Race for the Galaxy. Each of these three games have different mechanic for selecting a role on your turn, and the one used in Glory to Rome is a good one, but the other parts of the game just seem to miss that certain spark. I find the cards to be a little similar in the direction their effects push me and it frustrates me that I can't discard cards from the hand to the same degree that I can in San Juan or Race to the Galaxy. Often you'll find yourself being pushed in a direction you have no interest in going due to the cards in the pool and the cards in your hand. I think that's what creates my odd feeling about the game. So, it's good and worth multiple plays, but I thought it could be a little more. Rules do that annoying thing where they split essential information on the one mechanic into different sections, plus there's a few points still confusing that could have been elaborated on - out of town sites...

RATING: 8
Juego con mucha tensión que escala perfectamente a cualquier número de jugadores. La idea de que puedas ejecutar acciones de tus clientes, tanto en tu turno como en el turno de los demás, hace que no puedas despistarte un segundo y consigue eliminar el tiempo de espera entre turnos.

De todos modos es un gran juego, con bastante toma de decisiones y mucha tensión. Además la edición de Homoludicus me parece muy chula. Totalmente recomendable.

RATING: 8.75

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Each card can be used to lead an action or follow an action, be built for its text effect, or to be used as material for another building. It can represent bonus actions when placed as a client, be used as building material in your stockpile, score VPs and increase client and vault limits when built, score end-game VPs when in your vault, and be available for recycling after being played as actions into the pool. Not to mention  you need to time when you can think - draw cards - and make sure your hand is small when it can afford to be and big when you need to respond and go on the offensive, and when to sneak in a jack.

There are so many possibilities, that in this game, and unlike in other card games that aspire to be, like Dominion and Race for the Galaxy (where you know which 6-dev you're aiming for, and what it says on there), strategies grow organically. There is no set strategy to pursue, and you truly have to devise new uses and combos for the modular pieces in your hand at every given time. This is far and away the best of its genre.

"I'm thinking."

"I'm thinking!"

"I know!"

"Yes, I already did it!"

"Oh."[/i]

I like the multiple uses for each card.  I like how cards move through your hand in a manner different than most games (or at least it feels that way to me).  Our game seemed to end rather abruptly, but I think that was more a result of one player having things come out in a particularly advantageous order.  I look forward to playing again and expect to enjoy it even more.  

As an aside, the art doesn't really bother me.  Honestly, I'm kind of surprised at some of the comments directed towards the art.  Oh well, to each his own.  [01/08/2011]

RATING: N/A
2-5 3-4 2-5
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.6
GtR is a really cool, goofy game that uses cards in innovative ways.

Each card played on a player's turn selects an action, and all other players may also take this action if they play a matching card, following the lead player. This is similar, perhaps, to role selection in such games as Puerto Rico, San Juan, RftG, etc.

The actions allow players to acquire cards as 'goods' onto their player mats, which can then be sold for victory points or used to construct building that grant players special advantages and powers.

It is indeed these buildings which add excitement, variety, chaos and uncertainty into the smooth flow of the game and give GtR its somewhat dubious reputation for being unbalanced or 'broken'. I appreciate the wackiness of these special powers and feel they lend flavour and texture to this card game banquet.

The way the actions lead to winning is somewhat circuitous, so I would recommend playing (as the rule pamphlet suggests) a starter game, without the special building powers, when introducing this game to new players.

This game has entertained and intrigued my partner and me thoroughly over a few dozen plays (2 player); I strongly recommend it!

RATING: 6
Just one game, don't have a clue. Don't know what cards are in the deck, need to play some more. 

It's a San Juan/RFTG style game. Or so they say. I actually found the feel quite unique and the flow of the game intriguing - how the cards flow from your hand to discard pile to various places of player boards. It is optimisation thingy engine and doesn't have the card synergy of RFTG or the engine flow of Fleet, but has some amusing quirks on its own. Can only properly evaluate if I play it some more. I think some paths of the game weren't even explored that one time we played. 

The most interesting feature is the general flow of the cards, really weird and unique in particular how most cards have to get from your hand to the pile in order to be used again. Very intriguing. 

On graphic design: black box thingy. I'm not sure. On one hand it's pretty and clean - it's very clear which cards are where and makes it easier to follow the flow of the game. And it is evocative, but not of building Rome. The level of stylisations differs to much - some pictures are stylised (and those I like) but most are icons and while they're easy to read, they don't give you a picture of the place you're building. 
EDIT: went to check other artwork. Blah. This one is clean and easy to see what's going on.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Beneath the subdued graphics of the elusive Black Box edition lies a madcap card game of seemingly imbalanced abilities. Coupled with a tight network of actions, this seems like a recipe for disaster. But Glory to Rome somehow manages to pull it off, and with panache to boot. 

While players' personal strategies gradually solidify as building effects trigger, they have to continuously adapt to the changing game conditions as well. The cards you draw may suggest one option, but buildings in play could hint at another option. Players who keep track of the game's elements will statistically do better, although you do have the occasional outrageous combo that scoops the game – it's just how the game rolls.

Theme-wise, GtR is rather abstract and a difficult game to teach due to the confusing roundabout flow of actions. The fact that a player can be a runaway winner/loser is also a daunting prospect. 2P games suffer from a weakened Legionary action, while 5P games drag a little due to the sheer amount of information on board.

RATING: 6
(rated the original printing of the game)

Convoluted and dense card game (though mechanics are actually fairly simple once you get the hang of the phases and multiuse cards) that gives players the illusion of control. Shades of San Juan, Race for the Galaxy and card games of similar ilk abound.

The game ultimately drags on for a little too long with little payoff. The Merchant action seems a little overpowered and there are so many special cards that the rulebook has detailed explanations of them (not what you'd class as an elegant game design)

The art looks like cheap clipart and the card design is overly bright and somewhat...ugly. But the game works as it stands if that's any consolation.

RATING: 6
The game concept is very good. Quality and packaging are nice and slim and sturdy. I like all that.
Gameplay has much interaction, lots of humour, strategy (long-term planning), tactics (getting the stuff you need at the time you need it). All very good.
But it is quite chaotic at times (dont play when tired, not even a bit) and the "market" (open cards that one can choose from) can get quite messy.
The game has a steep learning curve, as there are many cards with special functions that need to be taken into consideration.
Rating might go up or down with more experience.

RATING: 6
[2011-08-12]
Nagyon vártam a magyar kiadását a játéknak, már régebben felfigyeltem rá milyen előkelő pontszámmal áll a BGG-n kártyajátékként. Hallottam, hogy a San Juanhoz, RFTG-hez hasonló, így nagyon kíváncsi voltam rá. Sajnos másokkal ellentétben én nem tudok ódákat zengeni róla. Meglepő módon a játék nekem még nehezebbnek is tűnt elsőre, mint a sokak által csak kínai jelkombinációnak tűnő ikonrendszerrel ellátott Race for the Galaxy. A Dicsőség Rómának játékban ugyanis egy lap jóval többfajta szerepet tölthet be, mint sci-fi rokonánál. Itt is szerepet választ a körön levő játékos, amit a többiek vagy követnek egy ugyanolyan lap kijátszásával a kezükből vagy elmélkedést választják, amivel tulajdonképpen laphoz jutnak. Egy lap lehet tehát szerep, lehet ügyfél, lehet nyersanyag, lehet kincs, illetve épületként is funkcionálhat. Ezek talán még nem túl komoly játékosnak is pár játék után átláthatóak lennének, de az egyes épületek számos különleges képességeinek és ezek kombinációjának, kivételeinek megtanulása jópár játékot igényel és úgy gondolom sok játék után is azt észben tartani, hogy ellenfeleink milyen különböző épülettel rendelkeznek komoly feladat még tapasztalt játékosok számára is. Nem tetszett, hogy a többfajta játék vége feltétel közül kettő is egy adott lap kijátszása, sőt ezek közül az egyik a játék végén kívül az adott játékos győzelmét is jelenti. A másik lap pedig tökéletesen alkalmas arra, hogy az adott játékos akkor fejezze be a játékot, amikor ő áll nyerésre, ami lehet akár a második kör is. Úgy érzem vannak túl erős és túl gyenge lapok is az épületek között, nem túl kiegyensúlyozottak így a szerencse szerepe az által, hogy kihez kerülnek a jobbak jelen van a játékban. Megmondom őszintén nekem a tanulóváltozat (ahol az épületek tulajdonságai nem számítanak) jobban tetszett, mint a teljes. Talán ha kevesebb különbözőfajta épület lenne jobban tetszene. A 2005-ös játékot rengeteg kritika érte az eredeti kiadás csúnya volta miatt, nos a magyar kiadás nagyon szép kivitelű, de talán a nyersanyagok hangsúlyosabb kinézetet kaphattak volna, illetve a fordítás sem lett tökéletes, de ettől eltekintve korrekten néz ki a játék. Nem rossz játék a Glory to Rome, de ha 7 Wonders egyszerű kártyajáték csak gémerkategóriában kapott jelölést az Év játéka díjra Németországban, akkor a Dicsőség Rómát nem is tudom hova kellene jelölni, mert jóval bonyolultabb. Persze ez ne riasszon el senkit, mert sok játék után biztosan pörgősebb, de új embereknek megtanítani nem könnyű feladat. Aki kedveli a San Juan, RFTG párost, az mindenképp adjon neki esélyt, ha teheti, de mindenképp egy komoly játékra számítson. A pontszámom nem végleges, az első játékélmény nem volt túl pozitív számomra, ezért kap még majd lehetőséget.

[2014-08-23]
Kapott második lehetőséget is, de abszolút nem változott a véleményem a játékról. Nem rossz, de kicsit túl van szerintem bonyolítva feleslegesen.
